      [default_constraint_naming_violation]

      [standard_definition]: "...where [default_constraints].[name] not like lower(N'' + [schemas].[name] + N'.' + [tables].[name] + N'.' + [columns].[name] + N'.default')"

      1. [dbo].[systranschemas].[typeid].[DF__systransc__typei__041093DD]
      2. [cdc].[change_tables].[partition_switch].[DF__change_ta__parti__06ED0088]
      3. [utility].[fruit].[persistent].[DF__fruit__persisten__147C05D0]
      4. [utility].[test_01].[persistent].[DF__test_01__persist__5F141958]

      [unique_constraint_naming_violation]

      [standard_definition]: "...where [indexes].[is_unique_constraint] = 1 and [indexes].[name] not like lower([schemas].[name] + N']' + [tables].[name] + N'.' + [columns].[name] + N'.unique')"

      1. [unbreakable_code].[flower].[flower].[unbreakable_code.flower.flower.unique]

      [primary_key_naming_violation]

      [standard_definition]: "...where [indexes].[is_primary_key] = 1 and [indexes].[name] not like lower([schemas].[name] + N'.' + [tables].[name] + N'.' + [columns].[name] + N'.primary_key_clustered')"

      1. [cdc].[change_tables].[object_id].[change_tables_clustered_idx]
      2. [cdc].[ddl_history].[object_id].[ddl_history_clustered_idx]
      3. [cdc].[ddl_history].[ddl_lsn].[ddl_history_clustered_idx]
      4. [cdc].[lsn_time_mapping].[start_lsn].[lsn_time_mapping_clustered_idx]
      5. [cdc].[captured_columns].[object_id].[captured_columns_clustered_idx]
      6. [cdc].[captured_columns].[column_ordinal].[captured_columns_clustered_idx]
      7. [cdc].[index_columns].[object_id].[index_columns_clustered_idx]
      8. [cdc].[index_columns].[index_ordinal].[index_columns_clustered_idx]
      9. [utility].[fruit].[fruit].[PK__fruit__1488762488771A16]
      10. [unbreakable_code].[flower].[id].[PK__flower__3213E83FFD872DBC]
      11. [repository_secure].[data].[id].[repository_secure.data.id.clustered_primary_key]
      12. [change_data_capture].[meta_data].[id].[change_data_capture.meta_data.id.clustered_primary_key]

      [no_primary_key_violation]

      [standard_definition]: No primary key on table. All tables must have a primary key.

      1. [repository_secure].[change].[]
      2. [utility].[test_01].[]

      [no_identity_column_violation]

      [standard_definition]: No identity column on table. Tables typically have an identity column. Evaluate manually whether this table is an exception to this common rule.

      1. This will not pick up the use of newsequentialid as a default in place of identity.
      2. There are cases where a surrogate primary key such as identity() is not preferred. You need to evaluate those individually.

      1. [cdc].[captured_columns].[]
      2. [repository_secure].[change].[]
      3. [cdc].[change_tables].[]
      4. [repository_secure].[data].[]
      5. [cdc].[ddl_history].[]
      6. [utility].[fruit].[]
      7. [cdc].[index_columns].[]
      8. [cdc].[lsn_time_mapping].[]
      9. [cdc].[repository_secure.data_CT].[]
      10. [dbo].[systranschemas].[]

      [no_unique_constraint_violation]

      [standard_definition]: No unique constraint on table. OLTP tables typically require a unique constraint that is separate from the primary key. This is because the primary key is typically a surrogate key to minimize page fragmentation and does not define uniqueness of the data.

      1. Tables containing only [xml] data cannot be constrained in this manner and must be constrained programmatically. See [repository_secure].[data] and [repository].[set] for examples.

      1. [dbo].[systranschemas]
      2. [cdc].[change_tables]
      3. [cdc].[ddl_history]
      4. [cdc].[lsn_time_mapping]
      5. [cdc].[captured_columns]
      6. [cdc].[index_columns]
      7. [utility].[fruit]
      8. [repository_secure].[change]
      9. [presentation].[test_without_constraints]
      10. [repository_secure].[data]
      11. [utility].[test_01]
      12. [cdc].[repository_secure.data_CT]
      13. [change_data_capture].[meta_data]

      [composite_primary_key_violation]

      [standard_definition]: Use of a composite primary key. Composite primary keys are often composite natural keys and lead to page fragmentation on inserts. OLTP tables should typically have a single surrogate primary key, with a unique constraint being used to define data uniqueness.

      1. [cdc].[captured_columns].[captured_columns_clustered_idx]
      2. [cdc].[ddl_history].[ddl_history_clustered_idx]
      3. [cdc].[index_columns].[index_columns_clustered_idx]

      [todo]
      [object_name]: [master].[dbo].[sp_get_best_practice_analysis]
      [description]:
      [master].[dbo].[sp_get_best_practice_analysis]

        Analyzes the current database for violation of best practice. Best practice evalutions include:

        1. [naming_violation] - The object does conform to standard naming convention.
        2. [no_primary_key_violation - The table does not include a primary key.
        3. [composite_primary_key_violation - The table uses a composite primary key. This typically indicateds that the key is a composite natural key. Recommended practice is to use a surrogate individual primary key on OLTP tables, only using a natural or composite natural primary key on OLAP tables.
        4. [no_identity_column_violation - The table does not include an identity column. All OLTP tables should include an identity column of either type [int] or [bigint].
        5. [no_unique_constraint_violation - The table does not include a unique index. All tables must include a unique index which defines the uniqueness of the table.

        Objects evaluated include:

        1. [DEFAULT_CONSTRAINT -
        2. [FOREIGN_KEY_CONSTRAINT -
        3. [PRIMARY_KEY_CONSTRAINT -
        4. [IDENTITY_COLUMN -
        5. [SQL_SCALAR_FUNCTION -
        6. [SQL_STORED_PROCEDURE -
        7. [SQL_TRIGGER -
        8. [UNIQUE_CONSTRAINT -
        9. [USER_TABLE -
      [execute_as]:

      --

      --select text of [bcp command] output and execute in command window. The extended properties are copied to a file as named in the bcp command.

      -------------------------------------------------------------------

      use [chamomile];

      go

      execute [dbo].[sp_get_best_practice_analysis];

      [unused_tables]

      [standard_definition]: Tables with a zero row count. Unused tables should be considered for deprecation.

      1. [repository_secure].[change]
      2. [presentation].[test_without_constraints]

      [low_row_count_tables]

      [standard_definition]: Tables with a row count of less than 5. Consider using a column constraint if the table is a meta data table. The additional complexity of joins to meta data tables may not be justified in this case.

      1. [presentation].[test_without_constraints]
      2. [repository_secure].[change]
      3. [change_data_capture].[meta_data]
      4. [utility].[fruit]
      5. [unbreakable_code].[flower]

      [unused_query_violation]

      [standard_definition]: Queries that have not been used for over 1 month. sys.dm_exec_procedure_stats - I like to identify the average amount of resources used for a single execution of a stored procedure. Calculating the average resources usage per execution allows you to more easily compare one stored procedure to another. To calculate these average resource usage numbers, I divide the total used number by the execution_count column. Here is some code where I used this technique to calculate average resources usage numbers for stored procedures that have metrics on my system.

      database_id cached_time last_execution_time execution_count total_worker_time / execution_count total_elapsed_time / execution_count total_logical_reads / execution_count total_logical_writes / execution_count total_physical_reads / execution_count
